# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy HTTP Filter Factory Registration and Instantiation

## Your Task

Trace how an HTTP filter factory is registered and instantiated per-connection in envoyproxy/envoy. Find C++ source files implementing: the filter factory registry, the NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory, the filter chain creation, and per-request filter instantiation.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)

Perfect! I've completed the comprehensive tracing of HTTP filter factory registration and instantiation in Envoy. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components Found:

### 1. **Filter Factory Registry**
- **NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory** (envoy/server/filter_config.h:273) - Base class for all HTTP filter factories with pure virtual `createFilterFactoryFromProto()` method
- Factories register themselves statically using `Registry::RegisterFactory` pattern

### 2. **Filter Chain Creation Infrastructure**
- **FilterChainManager** (envoy/http/filter_factory.h:70) - Interface for managing filter instantiation with `applyFilterFactoryCb()` method
- **FilterChainFactory** (envoy/http/filter_factory.h:89) - Interface with `createFilterChain()` method
- **HttpConnectionManagerConfig** (source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h) - Implements FilterChainFactory

### 3. **Filter Instantiation Per Connection**
- **FilterManager** (source/common/http/filter_manager.h:638) - Implements FilterChainManager, manages actual filter instances
- **FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl** (nested class in FilterManager) - Callbacks used to create and add filters to the chain
- **FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()** (source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:551) - Core method that invokes factory callbacks

### 4. **Configuration Processing**
- **FilterChainHelper** (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h:68) - Template class that processes filter configurations
- **processFilters()** and **processFilter()** methods iterate through configs and retrieve factories
- **FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()** - Applies pre-built filters to new connections

Filter Chain Creation Per Connection\\nWhen a new HTTP stream arrives at the connection manager, `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::createFilterChain()` (source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.cc:780) is called:\\n\\n- It calls `Http::FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()` (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.cc:17) with the pre-built `filter_factories_` list\\n- This utility iterates through each filter's config provider and calls `manager.applyFilterFactoryCb()` on the `FilterChainManager`\\n\\n## 4. Per-Request Filter Instantiation\\nThe `FilterChainManager` interface (envoy/http/filter_factory.h:70) is implemented by `FilterManager` (source/common/http/filter_manager.h:638):\\n\\n- `FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()` (source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:551) creates a temporary `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl` object\\n- It invokes the filter factory callback: `factory(callbacks)` - this is where the actual filter instance is created\\n- The callback typically calls `callbacks.addStreamDecoderFilter()` to instantiate the filter\\n- In `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl::addStreamDecoderFilter()` (source/common/http/filter_manager.h:918-922), the filter is wrapped in an `ActiveStreamDecoderFilter` and added to the decoder_filters_ list for this stream\\n\\nThis design separates factory registration (static, at startup) from filter instantiation (dynamic, per-request), allowing factory methods to be simple pure virtual functions that return configured callbacks, which are then invoked to create actual filter instances when needed.\"\n}\n",
